                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Good, moral or physical; anything that is good, real</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ideal,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">actual</hi> or <hi rend="ital">potential;</hi> and, being originally an inf. n., used as sing and pl.;] <hi rend="ital">a thing that all desire; such as intelligence,</hi> for instance, <hi rend="ital">and equity;</hi> (Er-Rághib, and so in some copies of the K;) [or <hi rend="ital">goodness;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and excellence; and what is profitable</hi> or <hi rend="ital">useful; benefit;</hi> (Er-Rághib;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَرٌّ</foreign>: (S, A, Msb:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">خُيُورٌ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) and also, accord. to the Msb,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11810-1" target="خِيَارٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11822"/></foreign>: (TA:) [but this latter seems to be properly pl. only of <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرٌ</foreign> used as an epithet (see below) and as a noun denoting the comparative and superlative degrees: it may however be used as an epithet in which the quality of a subst. is predominant:] <foreign lang="ar">خير</foreign> is of two kinds: namely, absolute <foreign lang="ar">خير</foreign>, which is <hi rend="ital">what is desired in all circumstances and by every person:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">what is</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خير</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">good</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to one and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شرّ</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">evil</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to another; as, for instance,</hi> (Er-Rághib,) <hi rend="ital">wealth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">property:</hi> (Zj, L in art. <foreign lang="ar">شد</foreign>, Er-Rághib, K:) it has this last signification, namely <hi rend="ital">wealth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">property,</hi> in the Kur, ii. 176 (S, TA) and ii. 274 and xxiv. 33 and xli. 49: or in the first and second of these instances it is thus called to imply the meaning of <hi rend="ital">wealth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">property, that has been collected in a praiseworthy manner,</hi> or it means <hi rend="ital">much wealth</hi> or <hi rend="ital">property;</hi> and this is its meaning in the first of the instances mentioned above, agreeably with a trad. of 'Alee; and also in the Kur, c. 8: (TA:) [being used as a pl. (as well as a sing.), it may be also rendered <hi rend="ital">good things:</hi>] and it is also used by the Arabs to signify <hi rend="ital">horses;</hi> (K, * TA;) and has this meaning in the Kur, xxxviii. 31: (TA:) [it is often best rendered <hi rend="ital">good fortune; prosperity; welfare; wellbeing; weal; happiness;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a good state</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition:</hi> and sometimes <hi rend="ital">bounty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beneficence.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ قَلِيلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الخَيْرِ</foreign> means [<hi rend="ital">A man possessing little,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no, good; possessing few,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no, good things;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">poor:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in whom is little,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">no, good</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goodness;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">niggardly:</hi> and also] <hi rend="ital">a man who does little good:</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">عص</foreign>:) or [<hi rend="ital">who does no good;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">who is not near to doing good;</hi> denoting the nonexistence of good in him. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">قل</foreign>.) [Thus it sometimes means the same as <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرَ فِيهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man in whom is no good or goodness; devoid of goodness; worthless.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">قِلَّةُ خَيْرٍ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Poverty:</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">niggardliness.</hi> (A and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">جحد</foreign>.) <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الخَيْرِ وَالخِيرِ</foreign> is explained voce <foreign lang="ar">خِيرٌ</foreign>. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَىيَدَىِ الخَيْرِ وَاليُمْنِ</foreign> [May it be <hi rend="ital">with the aid of good fortune and prosperity</hi>] is a prayer used with respect to a marriage. (A 'Obeyd, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّكَ مَا وَخَيْرًا</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">مَعَ خَيْرٍ</foreign>, i. e., <hi rend="ital">Mayest thou meet with, or attain, good.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرٌ</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ خَيْرٌ</foreign> resembles an epithet [like   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n11810-2" target="خَيِّرٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n11824"/></foreign>, and signifies <hi rend="ital">Good;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possessing good</hi>]; (Akh, S;) therefore the fem. is <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرَةٌ</foreign>, of which the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرَاتٌ</foreign>, (Akh, S, Msb, *) as occurring in the Kur, lv. 70; and they do not [there] mean by it [the comparative or superlative signification of the measure] <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَلُ</foreign>: (Akh, S:) you say

      <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ <ref cref="n11810-20" target="أَخْيَرُ" n="20" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF" select="n11826"/> مِنْكَ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">خَيْرُ</foreign>; and when you mean the signification of superiority, you say <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ خَيْرَةٌ النَّاسِ</foreign>, with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانَةُ خَيْرُهُمْ</foreign>, without <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>: but [SM says,] I know not how this is; for in the S is said what is different from this, and in like manner by Z in several places in the Ksh; and what is most strange is, that the author of the K quotes in the B the passage of J [from the S], and adopts the opinion of the leading authorities [as given in the S]: (TA:) or you say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانَةُ الخَيْرَةُ مِنَ المَرْأَتَيْنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a woman is the better of the two women</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ الخَيْرَةُ</foreign>, and

                  <hi rend="ital">Generousness; generosity;</hi> (S, A, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">liberality; munificence.</hi> (Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ ذُو خِيرٍ</foreign>
